Author: Ian McBride <imcbride@middlebury.edu>
Date:   Tue Aug 16 10:21:17 2016 -0400

    https://www.drupal.org/node/2401615  Require a specific placeholder format in db_query() in order to trigger argument expansion, and require explicit 'IN' parameter for conditions
    
    functions that accept SQL and pass it to db_query:
      - mm_retry_query()
      - GetTreeResults::__construct()
    
    functions that return SQL or put SQL in a variable passed by reference:
      - mm_content_get()
      - mm_content_get_query()
      - mm_content_get_accessible_nodes_by_mmtid_query()
      - _mm_search_result_query()
    
    mm_content_get()
      This function accepts an array as its first parameter that can contain an optional 'query' key. The value of this is a subquery that gets added to the statement on 1286. In searching, I couldn't find any instance where this key is passed to the function, but even so its conditions should be handled outside of the function. The first parameter will also have its other key value pairs added to the statement as conditions on lines 1327 and 1330, which handle the 'IN' case without using parameters.

    mm_content_get_accessible_nodes_by_mmtid_query()

      4767 uses join() to extract items for IN() rather than a named parameter

      4787 n.status is scalar
      4787 $scheduled already checked on 4772
      4787 $node_writeable already checked on 4782
      4798 $count_sql is assigned here

Date:   Tue Jan 3 13:42:56 2012 -0500

    r6186: When parsing an incoming URL, don't bother trying to join against mm_tree to as many levels as are present in the URL, if it is known that there are fewer levels actually in use in the tree. This avoids a problem where MySQL takes a huge amount of time to do lots of joins in one query.
    
    Also, reduce the maximum number of joins allowed to 40. Even though that is well below the theoretical limit of 61, it seems to be a tipping point in terms of performance.

commit 53e0bec1289355c27d0726a51a3dde4b603f47c0
Author: Adam Franco <afranco@middlebury.edu>
Date:   Mon Jun 13 13:43:36 2011 -0400

    DB-API: Updated _mm_browser_gallery_view() to use db_select().
    
    This is a pretty complicated query and I changed instances of
      SELECT FROM t1, t2 WHERE t1.nid = t2.nid
    to
      SELECT FROM t1 INNER JOIN t2 ON t1.nid = t2.nid
    
    as I believe that these should be equivalent since the comma syntax is equivalent
    to INNER JOIN and an inner join followed by the where clause give should be equivalent
    to an ON clause.

Author: Adam Franco <afranco@middlebury.edu>
Date:   Tue Jun 7 15:05:45 2011 -0400

    monster_menus_node_presave() now expects $node->owner to be an array().
    
    As of commit 8f1e457c1b0213449ae4412f0b0670fbddbd2739 (split up hook_nodeapi())
    installation of MM in a fresh Drupal 7 database would fail due to monster_menus_node_presave()
    expecting that $node->owner was an integer when in fact it was an array(uid => name).
    
    If verification that the account exists is not needed, then we could just use the
    $node->owner info directly rather than calling user_load().

    Temporarily commented out all usage of pager_query(). Revisit.
    
    This will need to be revisited and these queries re-written to use the db_select objects.
    
    To fix this there are two things to do:
    
      Extend the query:
        <?php
        $query = db_select('node', 'n')->extend('PagerDefault');
        ?>
      Next, define the number of rows per page:
        <?php
        $query->limit(10);
        ?>
